 from professionals and amateurs alike  &ndash;  to fill their appetite for mobile content (powered by new mobile broadband video capabilities).\",\"id\":27,\"image\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Faccel-com.s3.amazonaws.com\\u002Fuploads\\u002Ftop-of-mind\\u002Fd869c7bc20734d53939552921935e404\\u002FVideoTechnologydrone.jpg\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Learn More on YouTube\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Fwww.youtube.com\\u002Fwatch?time_continue=4&v=fMrWV128gZg\",\"locations\":\"none\",\"photoCredit\":\"\",\"position\":17,\"postType\":\"video\",\"slug\":\"Video\",\"sourceTitle\":\"DJI releases its new drone, the Mavic Pro | Crunch Report\",\"title\":\"Intelligent Machines\",\"videoId\":\"fMrWV128gZg\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E[Source: Philippe Botteri\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E, Accel]&nbsp;International expansion is a challenge any globally ambitious company will face &mdash; some sooner than others.\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWhile both the U.S. and Europe are consumer markets of more than 300 million people, grasping this potential in Europe is more challenging &mdash; and few companies have managed to do it successfully, given the region&rsquo;s many diverse, distinct markets. As a result, I&rsquo;m going to talk about international expansion using European examples and context for this piece &mdash; hopefully with takeaways that are universally relevant.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"9f0b\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EIs There Such A Thing As The &ldquo;Right Time&rdquo; To Launch In A New&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9e8d\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EThe first question the founding team of a consumer service needs to address concerns the timing of the launch in a new country. At McKinsey, and in most books on strategy, you will read that you can only replicate something successful, so you need to wait until your home country is cranking before starting abroad.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"cafa\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EThis is sound judgment. Unfortunately, it does not play out very well in the startup world. Why? Because by the time your model is a success in your home country, you&rsquo;ll already have other startups replicating your model in other key European markets, and competition gets fierce. As Nicolas Brusson, the co-founder of Blablacar puts it: \\u003Cem class=\\\"markup--em markup--p-em\\\"\\u003E&ldquo;By the time most European companies go international it is too late&hellip;We decided to go early into different European countries &mdash; adding a local team each time &mdash; before proving the business model, something very few players do.&rdquo;\\u003C\\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bffb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EOn the other hand, if you do a full roll-out with something that is not working or tuned enough, you will waste a lot of resources, which can sink the company.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"57b2\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003ESo when is the right time? Every company will have a different answer. In my view, given the current competitive environment, the sooner the better. However, it is critical to do it gradually and in a controlled manner.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EHere&rsquo;s how I advise startups to approach expansion:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"48df\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ENail your MVP (Minimum Viable Product) first\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have a service with a clear value proposition that works in different markets. You don&rsquo;t need bells and whistles, just something simple but effective.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9016\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EField test your product with a meaningful amount of customers\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E &mdash; typically a few thousands or tens of thousands. This should give you a good idea of what to expect.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"1a43\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EComplete your initial marketing playbook\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have identified acquisition channels (SEM, Facebook, offline&hellip;) at a reasonable cost with payback typically in less than nine months. Make sure your approach is scalable.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"0653\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EHow To Pick Your Next&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"efc5\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EOnce you&rsquo;re clear on the ideal time to launch in your next country, the question becomes &ldquo;where to go next?&rdquo;\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EWhile every business and situation are different, the following three elements should always be considered when choosing your next market:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"4259\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EMarket Potential:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E The &ldquo;market potential&rdquo; is a mix of different elements that must be weighted specifically for each business. It includes the market size, of course, but also the competitive dynamics, your network in the country (or your investor network) and the similarity with your home country. For example, in my experience, what works in France tends to also work well in Italy and Spain, but the U.K. can be an outlier.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"e8c1\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ECash Requirements:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Be clever with your resources. It is very important to assess your cost of capital and how much burn you can afford. If you raised &euro;20 million in your Series A, you can take more risks and launch abroad sooner than if you raised &euro;3&ndash;4 million. Picking a large market is attractive, but if it requires a level of investment that would reduce your runway considerably, you may be better off picking a smaller market. I have seen too many companies go big, burn big and then have to retrench, which is not a good position to be in.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"c943\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EHuman Capital:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Money is not everything; it is reasonably easy to get. The real challenge of international expansion lies in finding the right team, both at HQ to support the local launch and locally to scale the activity.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EI typically encourage companies to start their expansion with one country and digest it to the point where it is scaling before launching a new one. It does not mean you need to wait a couple of years &mdash; a few months may be enough.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"7f8a\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003EYou can then accelerate the number of launches over time if you are successful. It&rsquo;s key to remember that most technology markets are winner-takes-all &mdash; or at least takes most. It is, therefore, much better to be the leader in three countries than No. 5 in 10 countries.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bb16\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EAlso, the more countries you support, the higher your cash burn and the fewer resources you can allocate to win in a given market &mdash; this is something that needs constant evaluation.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"aabb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EIn summary, taking a thoughtful and considered approach to scaling internationally is key &mdash; and the sooner the better. First-mover advantage can offer a decisive advantage over competitors &mdash; and accelerate a company&rsquo;s ability to become the global category leader early on.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EWhile there may not necessarily be a perfect time for launching in a new market, preparing your business for expansion early on will support your continued success in a world where scaling internationally fast has become a requirement for any founder with global ambition.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Founders\",\"excerpt\":\"People have more opportunity to capitalize on their talents, wherever they are in the world. That lets them concentrate on their unique value-add rather than reinventing the wheel.\",\"id\":24,\"image\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Faccel-com.s3.amazonaws.com\\u002Fuploads\\u002Ftop-of-mind\\u002F137b31bc665244ac9989a01d1ff18e02\\u002FAPX_small.jpg\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Read more on TechCrunch\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Ftechcrunch.com\\u002F2015\\u002F03\\u002F18\\u002Fbattle-for-the-building-blocks\\u002F\",\"locations\":\"none\",\"photoCredit\":\"\",\"position\":8,\"postType\":\"image\",\"slug\":\"TheAPI-ificationOfBusiness\",\"sourceTitle\":\"Accel Bets Big On Startup-To-Startup APIs\",\"title\":\"The API-ification of business\",\"videoId\":\"\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E[Source: Fred Destin, Accel] I got a call from a brilliant young French entrepreneur the other day asking me about composing the board for his startup as he was closing his seed round. It seemed like every angel writing a check wanted to be on the board as well as some notable industry players. Here is what I told him: resist the pressure!\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for speed\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAs an early stage startup, speed is probably your core KPI. Of course you need to carefully consider your strategy given that you&rsquo;re acting with limited resources, but the reality is that you&rsquo;re having to make important decisions ALL the time. Recruitment, product, pricing, fundraising, co-founder issues, you name it. Having a tight group of board members allows you to convene a board at the drop of a hat and make informed decisions quickly. Aim for zero complexity in reporting, organising board meetings and making decisions. Speed will give you a decisive advantage, starting at the top.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for intimacy\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIn the early days of a company, having a very tight relationship with a small number of advisors will ensure that:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- any advice you receive is on point and highly informed\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can take real risks\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can change course on the fly\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EThe last thing you want is a mildly engaged board who doesn&rsquo;t fully understand the realities of your team and business and is likely to respond to fear as soon as the going gets tough. The ability for you as a founder to be totally transparent, including about your own fears and shortcomings, with a small group of engaged partners is key. It breeds the trust and for lack of a better work, intimacy, that you will need to thrive.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EIt&rsquo;s easier to add than to subtract\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIt&rsquo;s easy in the early days to yield to all the well-intentioned pressure to &ldquo;build a strong board&rdquo;. It&rsquo;s important to bear in mind though that it is much easier to add board members later on than ask an existing board member to leave &hellip; especially if your company is doing well. France is a particularly bad offender when it comes to massive boards. No one EVER wants to leave a successful company, and incoming investors are typically so clubby that they don&rsquo;t apply brute force to keep the board small. So you will routinely find Series B companies with 7 board members. I came across a consumer finance company recently that already had 9 (nine !) board members and was looking to add two. All the names looked great on paper, but I shuddered at the thought of having to sit through marathon reporting sessions with 11 people around the table. There is a time for structured governance and large boards, but seed ain&rsquo;t it. For SaaS companies, we found that MRR is the best metric on which to base sales commissions. While it may make sense to offer very slight adjustments for favorable payment terms and one time revenue, net additions to MRR should dominate the sales rep&rsquo;s thoughts. The reps&rsquo; top 3 priorities should be (i) MRR, (ii) MRR, and (iii) MRR.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EI had the opportunity to exchange on this topic with Gary Messiana, a BVP Entrepreneur-In-Residence and former VP Sales and CEO of Netli and he shared with me the basic structure he was using at Netli before the company was acquired last year by Akamai.&nbsp;When he initially built the sales compensation plan, he wanted the sales rep to think MRR and the most logical thing to do was to give $1 of commission for $1 of MRR sold. $1 of MRR generates $12 of annual revenue, so $1 commission equals 1\\u002F12=8.3% which is very close to the typical 8% paid for sales commissions.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EThe second thing he did was to define was the ramp up of the commission rate to make sure the best sales rep would get the most upside. As a result, I&rsquo;m going to talk about international expansion using European examples and context for this piece &mdash; hopefully with takeaways that are universally relevant.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"9f0b\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EIs There Such A Thing As The &ldquo;Right Time&rdquo; To Launch In A New&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9e8d\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EThe first question the founding team of a consumer service needs to address concerns the timing of the launch in a new country. At McKinsey, and in most books on strategy, you will read that you can only replicate something successful, so you need to wait until your home country is cranking before starting abroad.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"cafa\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EThis is sound judgment. Unfortunately, it does not play out very well in the startup world. Why? Because by the time your model is a success in your home country, you&rsquo;ll already have other startups replicating your model in other key European markets, and competition gets fierce. As Nicolas Brusson, the co-founder of Blablacar puts it: \\u003Cem class=\\\"markup--em markup--p-em\\\"\\u003E&ldquo;By the time most European companies go international it is too late&hellip;We decided to go early into different European countries &mdash; adding a local team each time &mdash; before proving the business model, something very few players do.&rdquo;\\u003C\\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bffb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EOn the other hand, if you do a full roll-out with something that is not working or tuned enough, you will waste a lot of resources, which can sink the company.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"57b2\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003ESo when is the right time? Every company will have a different answer. In my view, given the current competitive environment, the sooner the better. However, it is critical to do it gradually and in a controlled manner.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EHere&rsquo;s how I advise startups to approach expansion:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"48df\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ENail your MVP (Minimum Viable Product) first\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have a service with a clear value proposition that works in different markets. You don&rsquo;t need bells and whistles, just something simple but effective.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9016\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EField test your product with a meaningful amount of customers\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E &mdash; typically a few thousands or tens of thousands. This should give you a good idea of what to expect.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"1a43\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EComplete your initial marketing playbook\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have identified acquisition channels (SEM, Facebook, offline&hellip;) at a reasonable cost with payback typically in less than nine months. Make sure your approach is scalable.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"0653\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EHow To Pick Your Next&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"efc5\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EOnce you&rsquo;re clear on the ideal time to launch in your next country, the question becomes &ldquo;where to go next?&rdquo;\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EWhile every business and situation are different, the following three elements should always be considered when choosing your next market:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"4259\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EMarket Potential:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E The &ldquo;market potential&rdquo; is a mix of different elements that must be weighted specifically for each business. It includes the market size, of course, but also the competitive dynamics, your network in the country (or your investor network) and the similarity with your home country. For example, in my experience, what works in France tends to also work well in Italy and Spain, but the U.K. can be an outlier.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"e8c1\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ECash Requirements:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Be clever with your resources. It is very important to assess your cost of capital and how much burn you can afford. If you raised &euro;20 million in your Series A, you can take more risks and launch abroad sooner than if you raised &euro;3&ndash;4 million. Picking a large market is attractive, but if it requires a level of investment that would reduce your runway considerably, you may be better off picking a smaller market. I have seen too many companies go big, burn big and then have to retrench, which is not a good position to be in.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"c943\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EHuman Capital:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Money is not everything; it is reasonably easy to get. The real challenge of international expansion lies in finding the right team, both at HQ to support the local launch and locally to scale the activity.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EI typically encourage companies to start their expansion with one country and digest it to the point where it is scaling before launching a new one. It does not mean you need to wait a couple of years &mdash; a few months may be enough.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"7f8a\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003EYou can then accelerate the number of launches over time if you are successful. It&rsquo;s key to remember that most technology markets are winner-takes-all &mdash; or at least takes most. It is, therefore, much better to be the leader in three countries than No. 5 in 10 countries.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bb16\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EAlso, the more countries you support, the higher your cash burn and the fewer resources you can allocate to win in a given market &mdash; this is something that needs constant evaluation.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"aabb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EIn summary, taking a thoughtful and considered approach to scaling internationally is key &mdash; and the sooner the better. First-mover advantage can offer a decisive advantage over competitors &mdash; and accelerate a company&rsquo;s ability to become the global category leader early on.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EWhile there may not necessarily be a perfect time for launching in a new market, preparing your business for expansion early on will support your continued success in a world where scaling internationally fast has become a requirement for any founder with global ambition.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Founders\",\"excerpt\":\"People have more opportunity to capitalize on their talents, wherever they are in the world. Cloud services, internet commerce and viral marketing offer entrepreneurs the means to build disruptive companies from just about anywhere , from New York City to Bangalore and London to Helsinki.\",\"id\":35,\"image\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Faccel-com.s3.amazonaws.com\\u002Fuploads\\u002Ftop-of-mind\\u002Fb3498d53eaaa49099e623d7d4ceffa34\\u002FGlobal_entrepreneurship.jpeg\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Read more on TechCrunch\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Ftechcrunch.com\\u002F2015\\u002F11\\u002F20\\u002Fwhen-and-how-to-pick-your-next-launch-country\\u002F\",\"locations\":\"none\",\"photoCredit\":null,\"position\":19,\"postType\":\"image\",\"slug\":\"DistributedEntrepreneurship\",\"sourceTitle\":\"When And How To Pick Your Next Launch Country\",\"title\":\"Selecting your next launch country\",\"videoId\":\"\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E[Source: Accel] The social graph continues to reorient how people interact. After some great discussions that began at our OPEN conference last April, and with help from the community, we selected the OAS monicker to reflect the unique way in which open source software is&nbsp;\\u003Cem class=\\\"markup--em markup--p-em\\\"\\u003Eadopted\\u003C\\u002Fem\\u003E.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"19d8\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003ERather than clinging to proprietary software models of striving for profit right off the bat, or even to legacy open source models where vendors focus paid support for free software, successful OAS companies will carefully consider each phase of their growth in light of current open source trends. Here is what I told him: resist the pressure!\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for speed\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAs an early stage startup, speed is probably your core KPI. Of course you need to carefully consider your strategy given that you&rsquo;re acting with limited resources, but the reality is that you&rsquo;re having to make important decisions ALL the time. Recruitment, product, pricing, fundraising, co-founder issues, you name it. Having a tight group of board members allows you to convene a board at the drop of a hat and make informed decisions quickly. Aim for zero complexity in reporting, organising board meetings and making decisions. Speed will give you a decisive advantage, starting at the top.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for intimacy\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIn the early days of a company, having a very tight relationship with a small number of advisors will ensure that:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- any advice you receive is on point and highly informed\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can take real risks\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can change course on the fly\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EThe last thing you want is a mildly engaged board who doesn&rsquo;t fully understand the realities of your team and business and is likely to respond to fear as soon as the going gets tough. France is a particularly bad offender when it comes to massive boards. For SaaS companies, we found that MRR is the best metric on which to base sales commissions. While it may make sense to offer very slight adjustments for favorable payment terms and one time revenue, net additions to MRR should dominate the sales rep&rsquo;s thoughts. The reps&rsquo; top 3 priorities should be (i) MRR, (ii) MRR, and (iii) MRR.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EI had the opportunity to exchange on this topic with Gary Messiana, a BVP Entrepreneur-In-Residence and former VP Sales and CEO of Netli and he shared with me the basic structure he was using at Netli before the company was acquired last year by Akamai.&nbsp;When he initially built the sales compensation plan, he wanted the sales rep to think MRR and the most logical thing to do was to give $1 of commission for $1 of MRR sold. $1 of MRR generates $12 of annual revenue, so $1 commission equals 1\\u002F12=8.3% which is very close to the typical 8% paid for sales commissions.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EThe second thing he did was to define was the ramp up of the commission rate to make sure the best sales rep would get the most upside. To do that, he applied another simple rule:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 0-25% of the quota, $0.25 commision per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 25%-50% of the quota, $0.5 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 50%-75% of the quota, $1.0 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 75%+ of the quota, $1.5 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Saas\",\"excerpt\":\"Compensating the sales force is a difficult task and the key is usually to keep things simple, so that each sales rep knows what he needs to optimize to make more money at the end of the quarter. While it may make sense to offer very slight adjustments for\",\"id\":34,\"image\":\"\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Read more on Cracking the Code\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"http:\\u002F\\u002Fcracking-the-code.blogspot.co.uk\\u002F2009\\u002F01\\u002Fbuilding-your-saas-sales-compensation.html\",\"locations\":\"europe\",\"photoCredit\":null,\"position\":18,\"postType\":\"text\",\"slug\":\"BuildingYourSaaSSalesCompensationPlan\",\"sourceTitle\":\"Building Your SaaS Sales Compensation Plan\",\"title\":\"Building Your SaaS Sales Compensation Plan\",\"videoId\":\"\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"}],\"meta\":{\"limit\":1000,\"next\":null,\"offset\":0,\"previous\":null,\"totalCount\":26},\"pending\":false,\"complete\":true},\"topOfMind-{\\\"slug\\\":\\\"DistributedEntrepreneurship\\\"}\":{\"items\":[{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E[Source: Philippe Botteri\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E, Accel]&nbsp;International expansion is a challenge any globally ambitious company will face &mdash; some sooner than others.\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWhile both the U.S. and Europe are consumer markets of more than 300 million people, grasping this potential in Europe is more challenging &mdash; and few companies have managed to do it successfully, given the region&rsquo;s many diverse, distinct markets. As a result, I&rsquo;m going to talk about international expansion using European examples and context for this piece &mdash; hopefully with takeaways that are universally relevant.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"9f0b\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EIs There Such A Thing As The &ldquo;Right Time&rdquo; To Launch In A New&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9e8d\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EThe first question the founding team of a consumer service needs to address concerns the timing of the launch in a new country. At McKinsey, and in most books on strategy, you will read that you can only replicate something successful, so you need to wait until your home country is cranking before starting abroad.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"cafa\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EThis is sound judgment. Unfortunately, it does not play out very well in the startup world. Why? Because by the time your model is a success in your home country, you&rsquo;ll already have other startups replicating your model in other key European markets, and competition gets fierce. As Nicolas Brusson, the co-founder of Blablacar puts it: \\u003Cem class=\\\"markup--em markup--p-em\\\"\\u003E&ldquo;By the time most European companies go international it is too late&hellip;We decided to go early into different European countries &mdash; adding a local team each time &mdash; before proving the business model, something very few players do.&rdquo;\\u003C\\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bffb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EOn the other hand, if you do a full roll-out with something that is not working or tuned enough, you will waste a lot of resources, which can sink the company.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"57b2\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003ESo when is the right time? Every company will have a different answer. In my view, given the current competitive environment, the sooner the better. However, it is critical to do it gradually and in a controlled manner.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EHere&rsquo;s how I advise startups to approach expansion:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"48df\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ENail your MVP (Minimum Viable Product) first\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have a service with a clear value proposition that works in different markets. You don&rsquo;t need bells and whistles, just something simple but effective.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9016\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EField test your product with a meaningful amount of customers\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E &mdash; typically a few thousands or tens of thousands. This should give you a good idea of what to expect.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"1a43\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EComplete your initial marketing playbook\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have identified acquisition channels (SEM, Facebook, offline&hellip;) at a reasonable cost with payback typically in less than nine months. Make sure your approach is scalable.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"0653\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EHow To Pick Your Next&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"efc5\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EOnce you&rsquo;re clear on the ideal time to launch in your next country, the question becomes &ldquo;where to go next?&rdquo;\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EWhile every business and situation are different, the following three elements should always be considered when choosing your next market:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"4259\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EMarket Potential:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E The &ldquo;market potential&rdquo; is a mix of different elements that must be weighted specifically for each business. It includes the market size, of course, but also the competitive dynamics, your network in the country (or your investor network) and the similarity with your home country. For example, in my experience, what works in France tends to also work well in Italy and Spain, but the U.K. can be an outlier.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"e8c1\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ECash Requirements:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Be clever with your resources. It is very important to assess your cost of capital and how much burn you can afford. If you raised &euro;20 million in your Series A, you can take more risks and launch abroad sooner than if you raised &euro;3&ndash;4 million. Picking a large market is attractive, but if it requires a level of investment that would reduce your runway considerably, you may be better off picking a smaller market. I have seen too many companies go big, burn big and then have to retrench, which is not a good position to be in.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"c943\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EHuman Capital:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Money is not everything; it is reasonably easy to get. The real challenge of international expansion lies in finding the right team, both at HQ to support the local launch and locally to scale the activity.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EI typically encourage companies to start their expansion with one country and digest it to the point where it is scaling before launching a new one. It does not mean you need to wait a couple of years &mdash; a few months may be enough.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"7f8a\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003EYou can then accelerate the number of launches over time if you are successful. It&rsquo;s key to remember that most technology markets are winner-takes-all &mdash; or at least takes most. It is, therefore, much better to be the leader in three countries than No. 5 in 10 countries.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bb16\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EAlso, the more countries you support, the higher your cash burn and the fewer resources you can allocate to win in a given market &mdash; this is something that needs constant evaluation.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"aabb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EIn summary, taking a thoughtful and considered approach to scaling internationally is key &mdash; and the sooner the better. First-mover advantage can offer a decisive advantage over competitors &mdash; and accelerate a company&rsquo;s ability to become the global category leader early on.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EWhile there may not necessarily be a perfect time for launching in a new market, preparing your business for expansion early on will support your continued success in a world where scaling internationally fast has become a requirement for any founder with global ambition.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Founders\",\"excerpt\":\"People have more opportunity to capitalize on their talents, wherever they are in the world. Older, traditional industry incumbents took note, including 158-year old Northwestern Mutual, which acquired LearnVest in 2015 for $250 million. The acquisition marked an important moment in the finance industry as a legacy company embraced an innovative fintech startup in an effort to access the millennial market, while gaining access to new technology. Together with LearnVest, Northwestern Mutual deployed this technology across its portfolio of clients and financial Here is what I told him: resist the pressure!\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for speed\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EAs an early stage startup, speed is probably your core KPI. Recruitment, product, pricing, fundraising, co-founder issues, you name it. Speed will give you a decisive advantage, starting at the top.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003EOptimize for intimacy\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EIn the early days of a company, having a very tight relationship with a small number of advisors will ensure that:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- any advice you receive is on point and highly informed\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can take real risks\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E- you can change course on the fly\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EThe last thing you want is a mildly engaged board who doesn&rsquo;t fully understand the realities of your team and business and is likely to respond to fear as soon as the going gets tough. Global SaaS revenues are expected to grow by $19 billion in 2016, an increase of 22% from 2015, while traditional software revenues are shrinking by $10B. Two dollars in SaaS revenues are created for every $1 of software revenues eaten &ndash; an impressive stat, but where does Europe stand on the global SaaS map?\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cstrong\\u003ERising tide\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWhen I was in Silicon Valley, I spent most of my time investing in SaaS companies. When I moved back to Europe in 2011, I had to reduce my activity significantly in this area, as there was not enough going on. Five years later, the picture has changed drastically: five of Accel&rsquo;s 10 most recent investments in Europe have been SaaS companies. SaaS in Europe is exploding in terms of both quantity and quality. Our analysis estimates that the number of SaaS companies created has grown 4x between 2007-09 and 2013-15, and the amount raised by European SaaS companies has more than doubled. As it takes around 10 years for a SaaS company to reach maturity, the explosion we are seeing at the early stage has not yet translated into a significant number of exits. To date, there have been only four major European SaaS exits (all IPOs), including QlikTech in 2010, Wix in 2013, Zendesk in 2014 and Mimecast in 2015. The combined market cap of these companies today is around $9B.  from professionals and amateurs alike  &ndash;  to fill their appetite for mobile content (powered by new mobile broadband video capabilities).\",\"id\":27,\"image\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Faccel-com.s3.amazonaws.com\\u002Fuploads\\u002Ftop-of-mind\\u002Fd869c7bc20734d53939552921935e404\\u002FVideoTechnologydrone.jpg\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Learn More on YouTube\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Fwww.youtube.com\\u002Fwatch?time_continue=4&v=fMrWV128gZg\",\"locations\":\"none\",\"photoCredit\":\"\",\"position\":17,\"postType\":\"video\",\"slug\":\"Video\",\"sourceTitle\":\"DJI releases its new drone, the Mavic Pro | Crunch Report\",\"title\":\"Intelligent Machines\",\"videoId\":\"fMrWV128gZg\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E[Source: Fred Destin, Accel] Compensating the sales force is a difficult task and the key is usually to keep things simple, so that each sales rep knows what he needs to optimize to make more money at the end of the quarter. For SaaS companies, we found that MRR is the best metric on which to base sales commissions. While it may make sense to offer very slight adjustments for favorable payment terms and one time revenue, net additions to MRR should dominate the sales rep&rsquo;s thoughts. The reps&rsquo; top 3 priorities should be (i) MRR, (ii) MRR, and (iii) MRR.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EI had the opportunity to exchange on this topic with Gary Messiana, a BVP Entrepreneur-In-Residence and former VP Sales and CEO of Netli and he shared with me the basic structure he was using at Netli before the company was acquired last year by Akamai.&nbsp;When he initially built the sales compensation plan, he wanted the sales rep to think MRR and the most logical thing to do was to give $1 of commission for $1 of MRR sold. $1 of MRR generates $12 of annual revenue, so $1 commission equals 1\\u002F12=8.3% which is very close to the typical 8% paid for sales commissions.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003EThe second thing he did was to define was the ramp up of the commission rate to make sure the best sales rep would get the most upside. To do that, he applied another simple rule:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 0-25% of the quota, $0.25 commision per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 25%-50% of the quota, $0.5 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 50%-75% of the quota, $1.0 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp dir=\\\"ltr\\\"\\u003E- For 75%+ of the quota, $1.5 per $1 of MRR\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Saas\",\"excerpt\":\"Compensating the sales force is a difficult task and the key is usually to keep things simple, so that each sales rep knows what he needs to optimize to make more money at the end of the quarter. While it may make sense to offer very slight adjustments for\",\"id\":34,\"image\":\"\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Read more on Cracking the Code\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"http:\\u002F\\u002Fcracking-the-code.blogspot.co.uk\\u002F2009\\u002F01\\u002Fbuilding-your-saas-sales-compensation.html\",\"locations\":\"europe\",\"photoCredit\":null,\"position\":18,\"postType\":\"text\",\"slug\":\"BuildingYourSaaSSalesCompensationPlan\",\"sourceTitle\":\"Building Your SaaS Sales Compensation Plan\",\"title\":\"Building Your SaaS Sales Compensation Plan\",\"videoId\":\"\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E[Source: Philippe Botteri\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003Cspan id=\\\"docs-internal-guid-6a8e963a-08ae-ec7d-8bed-4df59a7ab835\\\"\\u003E, Accel]&nbsp;International expansion is a challenge any globally ambitious company will face &mdash; some sooner than others.\\u003C\\u002Fspan\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp\\u003EWhile both the U.S. and Europe are consumer markets of more than 300 million people, grasping this potential in Europe is more challenging &mdash; and few companies have managed to do it successfully, given the region&rsquo;s many diverse, distinct markets. As a result, I&rsquo;m going to talk about international expansion using European examples and context for this piece &mdash; hopefully with takeaways that are universally relevant.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"9f0b\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EIs There Such A Thing As The &ldquo;Right Time&rdquo; To Launch In A New&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9e8d\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EThe first question the founding team of a consumer service needs to address concerns the timing of the launch in a new country. At McKinsey, and in most books on strategy, you will read that you can only replicate something successful, so you need to wait until your home country is cranking before starting abroad.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"cafa\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EThis is sound judgment. Unfortunately, it does not play out very well in the startup world. Why? Because by the time your model is a success in your home country, you&rsquo;ll already have other startups replicating your model in other key European markets, and competition gets fierce. As Nicolas Brusson, the co-founder of Blablacar puts it: \\u003Cem class=\\\"markup--em markup--p-em\\\"\\u003E&ldquo;By the time most European companies go international it is too late&hellip;We decided to go early into different European countries &mdash; adding a local team each time &mdash; before proving the business model, something very few players do.&rdquo;\\u003C\\u002Fem\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bffb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EOn the other hand, if you do a full roll-out with something that is not working or tuned enough, you will waste a lot of resources, which can sink the company.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"57b2\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003ESo when is the right time? Every company will have a different answer. In my view, given the current competitive environment, the sooner the better. However, it is critical to do it gradually and in a controlled manner.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EHere&rsquo;s how I advise startups to approach expansion:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"48df\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ENail your MVP (Minimum Viable Product) first\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have a service with a clear value proposition that works in different markets. You don&rsquo;t need bells and whistles, just something simple but effective.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"9016\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EField test your product with a meaningful amount of customers\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E &mdash; typically a few thousands or tens of thousands. This should give you a good idea of what to expect.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"1a43\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EComplete your initial marketing playbook\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E. You need to have identified acquisition channels (SEM, Facebook, offline&hellip;) at a reasonable cost with payback typically in less than nine months. Make sure your approach is scalable.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Ch4 id=\\\"0653\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--h4 graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--h4-strong\\\"\\u003EHow To Pick Your Next&nbsp;Country?\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E\\u003C\\u002Fh4\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"efc5\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--h4\\\"\\u003EOnce you&rsquo;re clear on the ideal time to launch in your next country, the question becomes &ldquo;where to go next?&rdquo;\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EWhile every business and situation are different, the following three elements should always be considered when choosing your next market:\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"4259\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EMarket Potential:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E The &ldquo;market potential&rdquo; is a mix of different elements that must be weighted specifically for each business. It includes the market size, of course, but also the competitive dynamics, your network in the country (or your investor network) and the similarity with your home country. For example, in my experience, what works in France tends to also work well in Italy and Spain, but the U.K. can be an outlier.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"e8c1\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003ECash Requirements:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Be clever with your resources. It is very important to assess your cost of capital and how much burn you can afford. If you raised &euro;20 million in your Series A, you can take more risks and launch abroad sooner than if you raised &euro;3&ndash;4 million. Picking a large market is attractive, but if it requires a level of investment that would reduce your runway considerably, you may be better off picking a smaller market. I have seen too many companies go big, burn big and then have to retrench, which is not a good position to be in.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"c943\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003E\\u003Cstrong class=\\\"markup--strong markup--p-strong\\\"\\u003EHuman Capital:\\u003C\\u002Fstrong\\u003E Money is not everything; it is reasonably easy to get. The real challenge of international expansion lies in finding the right team, both at HQ to support the local launch and locally to scale the activity.\\u003Cbr \\u002F\\u003EI typically encourage companies to start their expansion with one country and digest it to the point where it is scaling before launching a new one. It does not mean you need to wait a couple of years &mdash; a few months may be enough.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"7f8a\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--pullquote\\\"\\u003EYou can then accelerate the number of launches over time if you are successful. It&rsquo;s key to remember that most technology markets are winner-takes-all &mdash; or at least takes most. It is, therefore, much better to be the leader in three countries than No. 5 in 10 countries.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"bb16\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p\\\"\\u003EAlso, the more countries you support, the higher your cash burn and the fewer resources you can allocate to win in a given market &mdash; this is something that needs constant evaluation.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp id=\\\"aabb\\\" class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EIn summary, taking a thoughtful and considered approach to scaling internationally is key &mdash; and the sooner the better. First-mover advantage can offer a decisive advantage over competitors &mdash; and accelerate a company&rsquo;s ability to become the global category leader early on.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\\r\\n\\u003Cp class=\\\"graf graf--p graf-after--p graf--last\\\"\\u003EWhile there may not necessarily be a perfect time for launching in a new market, preparing your business for expansion early on will support your continued success in a world where scaling internationally fast has become a requirement for any founder with global ambition.\\u003C\\u002Fp\\u003E\",\"category\":\"Founders\",\"excerpt\":\"People have more opportunity to capitalize on their talents, wherever they are in the world. Cloud services, internet commerce and viral marketing offer entrepreneurs the means to build disruptive companies from just about anywhere , from New York City to Bangalore and London to Helsinki.\",\"id\":35,\"image\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Faccel-com.s3.amazonaws.com\\u002Fuploads\\u002Ftop-of-mind\\u002Fb3498d53eaaa49099e623d7d4ceffa34\\u002FGlobal_entrepreneurship.jpeg\",\"imageCaption\":\"\",\"linkPrompt\":\"Read more on TechCrunch\",\"linkSource\":\"\",\"linkUrl\":\"https:\\u002F\\u002Ftechcrunch.com\\u002F2015\\u002F11\\u002F20\\u002Fwhen-and-how-to-pick-your-next-launch-country\\u002F\",\"locations\":\"none\",\"photoCredit\":null,\"position\":19,\"postType\":\"image\",\"slug\":\"DistributedEntrepreneurship\",\"sourceTitle\":\"When And How To Pick Your Next Launch Country\",\"title\":\"Selecting your next launch country\",\"videoId\":\"\",\"serviceName\":\"topOfMind\"},{\"body\":\"\\u003Cp\\u003E[Source: Accel] The social graph continues to reorient how people interact. We&rsquo;ve long believed in the Facebook-led narrative that change and opportunity come from expansive social networks.
